conversations. Scholars and teachers invite us to explore our inner lives in a
meaningful way. We are encouraged to take this inner learning and apply it
to our world outside. People may indeed solve problems and contribute to
their communities, families, and workplaces. But the missing piece here is
an explicit commitment to shifting unworkable systems and cultural norms.
Without intentional and proactive efforts to shift the context and rules of the
game that give rise to the problems we see and experience, these efforts
lead to only temporary results. They do not lead us to the essential public
discourses and subsequent action around war and peace, inequity, the
divisive notions of identities, the local, national, global forces of
concentration of wealth in the hands of a few.
Will we, as corporate, political, media, or government leaders, or think
tanks, have the humility and make the time to invest in our own and others’
learning in order to reverse the current inequities and planetary damage,
generate equitable and sustainable results, and create a paradigm shift? Will
we, as activists, source our and others’ inner capacities, deepen the
responses to challenges, and transform rage and frustration into principled
outrage? Will we, as teachers of the human potential movement, use our
influence to shift dysfunctional systems and cultural norms based on the
universal values of dignity, equity, and compassion?
Axiom 8. Systems Shifts and Root Factors Addressed
Systems change is frequently talked about. It is our recognition of the fact
that systems and cultural norms lie beneath the problems we face and wish
to solve. Although we refer to systems change, few know how to bring this
about in a simple and consistent way. Yet this work offers both meaning and
a methodology—it combines human greatness with systems thinking and
concrete solutions.
This is a design r-evolution—a paradigm shift through radical
evolutionary design.It is not enough to understand the factors and forces that create and
legitimize the systems and norms that inhibit progress. We must actively
design our work to shift these structures, systems, and cultural norms. And
we must know how to address the root factors of the challenges we face.
The entangled hierarchies that lead to complex problems require us to
address the full spectrum consciously. Most people are overwhelmed when
they think of shifting unworkable systems and cultural norms—working
with the multiple, nonlinear, interdependent factors appears far too
complicated! However, with a few design and operating principles and
templates, our response can be simple and not simplistic!
In today’s turbulent and complex times we have no choice but to navigate
in the different spheres where we engage. Three interrelated systems
spheres—societal norms, formal governance, and our workplace—require
us to source our inner capacities to deal with the root factors of
dysfunctional systems, bringing about the changes we wish to see.
We also operate in the context of societal, religious, and family norms.
Often, challenging unfair practices is hardest with those closest to us. We
described some of the threats to human beings and our planet, and a few
critical contributing factors to this plight, in the chapter on challenges and
our commitment to transform them. The stakes are high.
Am I seizing opportunities to make a difference in my work, whether in a
corporation, a government or nongovernmental organization, the media,
think tanks, or academia, or as a self-employed person? Am I leveraging
change in governance and political spheres as a concerned citizen? Every
situation, no matter how difficult, presents opportunities. Am I acting upon
them?
Axiom 9. Sophisticated Simplicity: Dealing with Complexity
The environment within which human development and a thriving planet
may occur is growing increasingly more complex. The pace of change has
accelerated, and there is a greater frequency of reforming and restructuring.
The consequences of error, oversight, misinformation, and miscalculation
are far-reaching and come swiftly. So are the consequences of positive and
skillful action. With the immense advances in technology and connectivity,
life-enhancing strategies and actions move results more rapidly.
Globalization, digitization, demographic shifts, and rapid environmental
degradation are all creating waves of change requiring us to understand
development challenges differently—and respond accordingly. Human
development, or the lack thereof, relates to complex social phenomena
within which we are called to help unleash the resources we have in service
of all peoples. The persistent manifestations of poverty, high mortality,
hunger, conflict, war, and exploitation are symptoms of social dysfunction
and deeper-lying cultural forces.
Once we understand this, it becomes more readily clear why these
development problems persist. What steps will you take to ensure that our
technology and other resources address these issues successfully at home, in
society, and at work, and as soon as possible?
Axiom 10. Going to Scale—The Unfinished Business
The conscious full-spectrum response is a fractal of a radical new field
where ethical leadership is the norm. We partner differently and align work
to generate equitable and sustainable transformation. As a participant once
said, “I now see possibilities where earlier there was hopelessness. But we
are far from where we need to be.”
Let us ride on the waves of new thinking. Let us move from relentless
growth to prosperity without growth; from only survival strategies to
thriving; from opulent wealth to sophisticated simplicity with abundance.Let us transcend polarities and go beyond Democrats or Republicans;
beyond Christians or Muslims! Let us align for synergy and
interdependence.
It is time to deconstruct the locus of power that divides us as adults and
children, as bosses and employees, as Westerners and non-Westerners, as
religious and nonreligious, as nationals and immigrants, as billionaires and
poor people. When we are able to truly listen and see the other’s
perspective, there is an opening for profound change to take place.
Once we apply the transformative alchemic praxis in our everyday life
and work, it becomes a moment-to-moment way of BEING at home, at
work, with our friends, in our community, and in society. Every action is a
fractal that results in prosperity.
Do you truly recognize the magnitude and underlying factors of our
problems today? Are you willing and able to use transformative design
templates to create the architecture of equitable and sustainable change?
Will you choose to understand and act upon what is equitable and
transformative and integrate it into your daily life and work? And are you
called to step up and offer your learning and action in service of humanity
and our planet?
We are the ones we have been waiting for. Creating new patterns requires
that we connect to who we truly are, rising above our fears in order to
pursue and realize our vision for dignity, justice, and peace in our lifetime.
The most difficult part is our own discipline to practice. It is so easy to fall
back into our habitual patterns and continue working in the ways we have
been taught. Self-generating pathways require us to constantly renew
ourselves. The path is never linear, the solution is never obvious or unique:
we will make a difference only when we truly inquire into ourselves and
our world, taking it upon ourselves to shift what is not working. Doing
anything less would be giving up on ourselves, our families, our
communities, our children, and the generations to come.

About the Author
Monica Sharma, trained as a physician and epidemiologist, worked for the
United Nations more than twenty years. Currently, she engages worldwide
as an international expert and practitioner on leadership development for
sustainable and equitable change. She works with United Nations,
Universities, for example, the University of Virginia and Johns Hopkins,
management institutions, governments, businesses, media, and civil society
organizations. She is the Tata Chair Professor at the Tata Institute of Social
Sciences in Mumbai. She has published and presented over 250 articles in
journals and international forums.
Monica Sharma created and uses a unique response model based on
extensive application—a conscious full-spectrum model—which is for
simultaneously solving problems, shifting systems, and creating new
patterns sourced from individual inner capacity and transformational
leadership. This model has generated sustainable results worldwide.
www.radicallytransform.org
About North Atlantic Books
North Atlantic Books (NAB) is an independent, nonprofit publisher
committed to a bold exploration of the relationships between mind, body,
spirit, and nature. Founded in 1974, NAB aims to nurture a holistic view of
the arts, sciences, humanities, and healing. To make a donation or to learn
more about our books, authors, events, and newsletter, please visit
www.northatlanticbooks.com.
North Atlantic Books is the publishing arm of the Society for the Study
of Native Arts and Sciences, a 501(c)(3) nonprofit educational
organization that promotes cross-cultural perspectives linkingscientific, social, and artistic fields. To learn how you can support us,
please visit our website.
